      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846558917" href="/book/show/23346377-in-a-dark-dark-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296178083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5154980853958347656">After reading the blurb, I was dying to get my hands on this book. Can you blame me? It promised suspense, shock and the frantic page-turning quality of any good thriller. Unfortunately, it didn’t totally deliver. Not for me, at least. <br/><br/>It was slow starting, which I won’t totally knock it for, but there was no shocking revelation to me in regards to who was behind it all or even the ending. I saw it coming a mile away and in no way did I find the story even remotely creepy. <br/><br/>Even after all of that</span>
  <span id="freeText5154980853958347656" style="display:none">After reading the blurb, I was dying to get my hands on this book. Can you blame me? It promised suspense, shock and the frantic page-turning quality of any good thriller. Unfortunately, it didn’t totally deliver. Not for me, at least. <br /><br />It was slow starting, which I won’t totally knock it for, but there was no shocking revelation to me in regards to who was behind it all or even the ending. I saw it coming a mile away and in no way did I find the story even remotely creepy. <br /><br />Even after all of that, it’s not that I hated the book, I’ve just read others that I felt were more compelling and surprising. To put it bluntly - I've read better. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5154980853958347656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1336746823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1336746823" />
    <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books"><img alt="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550077760p2/16912659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1336746823?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books">Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846558917" href="/book/show/23346377-in-a-dark-dark-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1336746823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3712840979592293928"> ***MS. WARE HAS A NEW BOOK COMING OUT ON 8/8/20, READ THIS ONE FIRST***<br/><br/>Leonara Ware has constructed for herself a solitary existence in London, living in a small but comfortable apartment, writing crime novels and eating, running and writing on a very precise schedule. She seems content for the moment but we wonder why she is so sheltering herself from others her own age and not really living her life.<br/><br/>She receives an invitation to a hen weekend (we in the States call it a bachelorette party) fo</span>
  <span id="freeText3712840979592293928" style="display:none"> ***MS. WARE HAS A NEW BOOK COMING OUT ON 8/8/20, READ THIS ONE FIRST***<br /><br />Leonara Ware has constructed for herself a solitary existence in London, living in a small but comfortable apartment, writing crime novels and eating, running and writing on a very precise schedule. She seems content for the moment but we wonder why she is so sheltering herself from others her own age and not really living her life.<br /><br />She receives an invitation to a hen weekend (we in the States call it a bachelorette party) for a former friend, Clare, whom she has not seen for 10 years. After much deliberation and only after having been assured that her other friend Nina will also be attending she agrees to go.<br /><br />The book is told in past and present sequence with Nora being in hospital with a serious head injury and multiple cuts and bruises. The police keep urging her to remember what happened the last night of the hen weekend when things went horribly wrong. She knows that someone is dead because she overhears the police but at first her memory eludes her.<br /><br />Upon her arrival at the hen party, taking place in a beautifully crafted glass house owned by a friend’s aunt, she soon finds out that Clare has invited her to tell her that she is marrying James, Nora’s ex-boyfriend. The other guests include, Flo, a woman who seems to worship Clare, Tom, a friend from Clare’s theater group and Melanie a young mother who was reluctant to leave her infant home.<br /><br />Nora soon is feeling so uncomfortable that she feels a run will clear her mind. She runs through the “dark, dark woods” and does feel somewhat better after.<br /><br />Nevertheless the first night passes uncomfortably with Flo constantly trying to make this the perfect night for Clare and the others being incredibly bored. There is no cell reception in the house and inexplicably the landline is cut off. Melanie decides to return home not being able to tolerate being cut off from her husband and young child.<br /><br />The plot becomes more tense and tightly woven and what seemed at first to be a predictable thriller evolves into a novel that is readable, frightening and well written. <br /><br />The scenes in the hospital with Nora struggling to remember what happened and the police bearing down on her as a suspect were the most tense for me. Within a few days she does remember and what follows next is a riveting attempt by Nora to return to the house and reclaim her memory.<br /><br />I read this book in a couple of sessions finding that it did keep me turning pages and trying to find the murderer among the group.<br /><br />Even though the plot is not wholly original (I’ve read other stories taking place in the woods with a killer among a group) I found the writing to be very good. Very good descriptions of the landscape and house and good character development. I will be recommending this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3712840979592293928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14020441219534907039">Update: 9/2018<br/>Now I have read another of her works. I found it to be about as good as this one (The Death of Mrs. Westaway). <br/><br/>I also wanted to add that, yes, this one may seem scattered at first because the character has no memory.   <span id="freeText14020441219534907039" style="display:none">Update: 9/2018<br />Now I have read another of her works. I found it to be about as good as this one (The Death of Mrs. Westaway). <br /><br />I also wanted to add that, yes, this one may seem scattered at first because the character has no memory. She and you, the reader, are piecing it together; so of course it’s not going to be tra la, la, here, let me hand you the story ! It builds! Yesss! Nifty little device. Only for those with patience. <br />***********<br /><br />I should write a proper review for this now that I have read three of her books. I have to say, that I favor this one the most. It came at me from the opening sentence and beckoned me to begin piecing things together as I went along. The author likes to switch point of view so you can see a bit of everyone - or is it just enough of some- to give you hints and ideas, but in this book she does it the very least out of all three. <br />Out of all three books, the mystery in each that pieces together, how the cards fall; this book is the most cathartic to me and also makes the most sense. <br />I'm glad I own this one. I can loan it out or reread it. I think it is aptly named. <br />This is not to say the other two won't blow your minds either. This one is just, my cup of tea. ;)<br />Clink*</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3007150011" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10348019190301289693">A solid if ultimately unoriginal thriller. It has a good enough mystery, simple and relatively easy to guess, but it’s a pretty good recommendation for those who grew up reading Agatha Christie or even just Nancy Drew. I don’t really understand the theming of the “dark, dark wood” story, this is just a murder mystery with an unreliable narrator. If you’re into the simplicity of that then maybe this will work, and that was enough for me to really enjoy the reading experience. <br/><br/>I do think it was be</span>
  <span id="freeText10348019190301289693" style="display:none">A solid if ultimately unoriginal thriller. It has a good enough mystery, simple and relatively easy to guess, but it’s a pretty good recommendation for those who grew up reading Agatha Christie or even just Nancy Drew. I don’t really understand the theming of the “dark, dark wood” story, this is just a murder mystery with an unreliable narrator. If you’re into the simplicity of that then maybe this will work, and that was enough for me to really enjoy the reading experience. <br /><br />I do think it was beyond cliched to make this about a crime writer, though. Seriously? Of all professions, lol. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846558917" href="/book/show/23346377-in-a-dark-dark-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=liburrrrrry-book">liburrrrrry-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=lifetime-stabby-stabs-for-women">lifetime-stabby-stabs-for-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=pretty-on-the-outside">pretty-on-the-outside</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209115427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12155978344039189330">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars<br/><br/>I haven’t been able to break the “10 reviews behind” mark these last couple of months and since this one already has 10,000 it probably doesn’t need whatever idiocy I can spew out about it to help sell more copies, so I’m going to barf out something real quick here in order to (hopefully) not spend the first half of 2018 trying to play catch up. <br/><br/><i>In A Dark Dark Wood</i> is a book that I spent the better part of the year waiting for</span>
  <span id="freeText12155978344039189330" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br />3.5 Stars<br /><br />I haven’t been able to break the “10 reviews behind” mark these last couple of months and since this one already has 10,000 it probably doesn’t need whatever idiocy I can spew out about it to help sell more copies, so I’m going to barf out something real quick here in order to (hopefully) not spend the first half of 2018 trying to play catch up. <br /><br /><i>In A Dark Dark Wood</i> is a book that I spent the better part of the year waiting for my turn to come around at the library. Miracle of all miracles, somehow I managed to remember that I wanted to read this simply due to the title/cover, but also managed to not spoil myself about anything regarding the story. That’s probably a good thing, because even though in the back of my brain I knew this was a mystery, when I settled down to read it one dreary Saturday morning I got lost in the story and gave zero farts about trying to figure out all of the whos/whens/whats/whys/hows. I was just kind of digging the goings on at the Hen Weekend. <br /><br />If you’re looking for a real thrill-ride of a book, you might find yourself disappointed. The actual “whodunit” and other reveals were exactly what I thought they would be having watched Lifetime Television for Women for a bigly amount of years. What made this one work was all in the storytelling.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12155978344039189330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2695071508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2695071508" />
    <a title="Stephanie Nicholas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92879415-stephanie-nicholas"><img alt="Stephanie Nicholas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548828666p2/92879415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2695071508?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Nicholas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Nicholas" href="/user/show/92879415-stephanie-nicholas">Stephanie Nicholas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2695071508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3139906776190718244">Leonora (Nora) is summoned by her best friend's maid of honor to attend a hen do (bachelorette weekend) in the English countryside. It's strange, though, because she hasn't even been invited to the wedding. She contacts another one of her University friends, Nina, and they make a pact to go together. Not soon after they arrive, Nora has the past dredged up by other invitees, and all becomes very awkward. She thinks of leaving, but when one of the other women goes home early, she feels obliged to</span>
  <span id="freeText3139906776190718244" style="display:none">Leonora (Nora) is summoned by her best friend's maid of honor to attend a hen do (bachelorette weekend) in the English countryside. It's strange, though, because she hasn't even been invited to the wedding. She contacts another one of her University friends, Nina, and they make a pact to go together. Not soon after they arrive, Nora has the past dredged up by other invitees, and all becomes very awkward. She thinks of leaving, but when one of the other women goes home early, she feels obliged to stay. She soon wishes she had left anyway, because the wheels come off. Way off.<br /><br />This was not Ruth Ware's strongest novel. I found much of the second half implausible and thrown together without enough forethought. However, because of the relationship dynamics of the friends, and the suspense, it was utterly unputdownable. <br /><br />If you're looking for a strong plot, you won't find it here. If you're looking for an atmospheric thriller, I can't contest, this ought to be read. <br /><br />This, for me, was a tough book to rate. 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3139906776190718244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1377524219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377524219" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1377524219?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781501112317" href="/book/show/23783496-in-a-dark-dark-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1377524219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1458532496903002224">I was expecting something a little more original when picking this up. But sadly it fell into the same rote, formulaic structure of most 'unreliable narrator' murder mysteries these days. The writing was decent but definitely nothing spectacular, and it couldn't redeem the book from being anything but ordinary. It's not a bad book by any means, but if you've read <i>Gone Girl</i> or <i>The Girl on the Train</i> you won't find anything particularly special here. Sure, it was enjoyable enough, but by the last t</span>
  <span id="freeText1458532496903002224" style="display:none">I was expecting something a little more original when picking this up. But sadly it fell into the same rote, formulaic structure of most 'unreliable narrator' murder mysteries these days. The writing was decent but definitely nothing spectacular, and it couldn't redeem the book from being anything but ordinary. It's not a bad book by any means, but if you've read <i>Gone Girl</i> or <i>The Girl on the Train</i> you won't find anything particularly special here. Sure, it was enjoyable enough, but by the last third of the book or so I just wanted to know what happened and be done. I'll admit I didn't totally see the ending coming, but the way in which it was presented didn't leave me completely shocked either. At the end it was just a mediocre mystery story that one could do without having read, unless you're new to the genre. However, I found most of it to be predictable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1458532496903002224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3964962280401779174" style="display:none">A creepy hen-party, a few unlikely invitees. A secret agenda. A spooky glass house. An atmospheric forest. <br /><br />Entertaining: yes<br />Psychological thriller: yes<br />Predictable: yes<br />Programmatic: yes<br />Cover: magnificent!<br /><br />A middle-of-the-road novel. A good read, and for some, a surprising ending. But I saw the ending coming in the beginning. The drawn-out denouement was annoyingly contrived - to keep the suspense up was just too obvious. And the so-called secret was also clear from the start. Yawn.<br /><br />And that's it. Nevertheless, a cozy read.<br /><br />Two stars mean it was so-so. Three stars: The prose was good.</span>

		    <b>
          <a title="The Sunshine Girls Book Club/ Tyler´s Book Club" class="actionLink" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/21761204-december-book-of-the-month">The Sunshine Girl...:</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Yl+TnVKquYHZ8ytVQPw2dCavwINlwoi9F+4STUmCwdlboHMfIQ93Js1C/mogui8ui2wCX5+Wi7hwAdIwBk3agA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mGE83RRatvbx3mPG319gEd5qOW7cRBW33pIicpeV9W6hntxfZ/94UeVvtvm/GXlLc6n7siYQFrK5feIP2FruNw==')})
  }

The cops think her memory loss is highly convenient, and they suspect she was up to no good. \n\nKaren returns home with Tom, determined to heal and move on with her life. Then she realizes something’s been moved. Something’s not quite right. Someone’s been in her house. And the police won\'t stop asking questions.\n\nBecause in this house, everyone’s a stranger. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6523531168146860576">Ruth Ware grew up in Sussex, on the south coast of England. After graduating from Manchester University she moved to Paris, before settling in North London. She has worked as a waitress, a bookseller, a teacher of English as a foreign language and a press officer. She is married with two small children, and In a Dark, Dark Wood is her début thriller.<br/><br/>Find her on twitter at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.twitter.com/ruthwarewriter'>www.twitter.com/ruthwarew</a></span>

She has worked as a waitress, a bookseller, a teacher of English as a foreign language and a press officer.
